Topic: Math
Question: A company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month, at a production cost to the company of $110 per component, and sells all of the components by the end of each month. What is the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) will be at least $626,400 ?
Choices:
  A: 226
  B: 230
  C: 240
  D: 260
  E: 280
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The company produces and sells 420 components every month. 
  The production cost per component is $110. 
  The yearly profit should be $626,400 at least. 

Calculation: 
  Yearly production cost = 110 * 420 * 12 = $554,400
  Minimum revenue required = yearly production cost + 626,400 = 554,400 + 626,400 = $1,180,800
  Minimum selling price per component = 1,180,800 / (420 * 12) = 233.33 ≈ $234

Round up to the nearest whole number, we get the answer:
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month.
  - The production cost to the company of each component is $110.
  - The yearly profit is the revenue from sales minus production costs.
Action: 
  Let's first calculate the yearly production costs = 420 units/month * $110/unit * 12 months/year = $554,400/year.
  To get a yearly profit of $626,400, the yearly revenue from sales should be $1,180,800 ($1,180,800 - $554,400 = $626,400).
  To find the minimum selling price, we simply need to divide the yearly revenue by the number of units produced per year:
  $1,180,800/year ÷ (12 months/year * 420 units/month) = $230/unit
  Therefore, the answer is (B) $230.

Question: If m > 0, y > 0, and x is m percent of 4y, then, in terms of y, m is what percentage of x?
Choices:
  A: y/400
  B: 4y
  C: 50y
  D: 2500/y
  E: 5000/y
Response 0:

  To solve the problem, we need to translate the given information into an equation and then simplify the equation to solve for m in terms of y.
  Using algebra, we can manipulate the given equation to express m in terms of x and y, and then solve for m as a fraction of x.
  One possible method is to write:
  x = m/100 * 4y
  m/100 = x / (4y)
  m = 100x / (4y)
  m = 25x / y
  This means that m is 25 times x divided by y, or 25 times the ratio of x to y. Therefore, the answer is a fraction that involves 25 as a factor.
  A: y/400 is not equivalent to 25x/y.
  B: 4y is not equivalent to 25x/y.
  C: 50y is not equivalent to 25x/y.
  D: 2500/y is equivalent to 100x/y, which is not the same as 25x/y.
  E: 5000/y is not equivalent to 25x/y.

  Therefore, m is (25/y) * 100 percent of x.

Question: A sales person gets a 10% commission on each sale he makes. How many sales of $250 each must he make in order to reach a salary of at least $1000?

  B: 24
  C: 25
  D: 40
  E: 52

  The total commission earned is proportional to the total sale price.
  The salesperson's salary is equal to the total commission earned.

  Let's call the number of sales needed "n".
  The total commission earned is n * $25.
  We need to solve for n when the total commission is at least $1000.
  So we can set up the following equation: n * $25 >= $1000.
  We can divide both sides by $25 to get n >= 40.
  Since we can't have a fractional number of sales, the smallest integer value of n that satisfies this inequality is 40.

Topic: Math
Question: What should come in place of the question mark(?) in each of the following questions ?
a2 - b2/(a + b)2 (?)=(a - b)2
Choices:
  A: (a + b)(a - b)
  B: (a - b)2
  C: (a + b)2
  D: a3 + b3
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  a2 - b2 can be factored as (a + b)(a - b)
  (a + b)2 can be expanded as a2 + 2ab + b2
  (a - b)2 can be expanded as a2 - 2ab + b2

Using the formula of (a - b)2
(a + b)(a - b)/(a + b)2 = (a - b)2/(a + b)2
(a - b)2/(a + b)2 = (a - b)2/(a + b)2

This equation is already in the required form which is (a - b)2.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
The given expression is a difference of squares and can be simplified by using the identity (a-b)(a+b)=a^2-b^2.

a^2 - b^2/(a + b)^2 = (a^2 - b^2)/(a + b)^2 = [(a-b)(a+b)]/(a+b)^2 = (a-b)/(a+b) * (a-b)/(a+b) = (a-b)²/(a+b)²

By substituting the above simplification in the given expression, we get:

(a-b)²/(a+b)² = (a-b)²

Therefore, the answer is (a-b)².

Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
We can solve this problem using the following identity:
a²-b² = (a+b)(a-b)

a²-b²/(a+b)² = (a²-b²) / (a+b)² (by taking common denominator)
= [(a+b)(a-b)] / (a+b)² (using the above identity)
= (a-b)/(a+b)  (simplifying the expression)

Now compare this simplified expression with the given expression: (a-b)²/(a+b)²
We can see that both expressions are same, so the answer is (a-b)²/(a+b)² = (a-b)/(a+b)

To solve the given expression:

Cancel out the common factor (a + b) on both sides:
(a - b)/(a + b) = (a - b)2/(a + b)2

Cross-multiply:
(a - b)(a + b)2 = (a - b)2(a + b)

Simplify and cancel out (a - b) on both sides:
(a + b)2 = (a - b)

We can see that the expression simplifies to (a + b)2 = (a - b)2
Therefore, the answer is (a - b)2

Question: M = abc is a three digit number and N = cba, if M > N and M - N + 396c = 990. Then how many values of M are more than 300.

  B: 30

  D: 200
  E: None

  - The letters a, b, and c represent the digits of a three-digit number, where a is the hundreds digit, b is the tens digit, and c is the ones digit.
  - The number M can be found by multiplying a, b, and c, whereas the number N is formed by arranging the digits of M in reverse order.
  - If M > N, then a > c, or a = c and b > b.
  - M - N is equal to 99(a-c) - 9(b-b), which simplifies to 99(a-c) - 9(b-b) = 99(a-c) - 9(b-b).

Question: A cyclist travels at 12 miles per hour. How many minutes will it take to travel 48 miles?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 240
  C: 30
  D: 60
  E: 120
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  We can use the formula: time = distance / speed
  The cyclist's speed is 12 miles per hour
  The distance to be travelled is 48 miles.
  We need to convert the answer to minutes.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  To solve for time, we can use the formula: time = distance / rate.
  The rate is given as 12 miles per hour.
  The distance is given as 48 miles.
  
Action: 
  time = distance / rate
  time = 48 miles / 12 miles per hour
  time = 4 hours
  Convert hours to minutes: 4 hours * 60 minutes per hour = 240 minutes
  Answer("B")

  If the median income is $3000, it means that half of the family members earn less than $3000, and the other half earns more than $3000.
  Let's assume that x family members earn more than $3000 and x family members earn less than $3000.
  The total number of family members is 2x.
  The total income is $9000, so we can write the following equation:
  x*$3000 + x*$3000 = $9000
  2x*$3000 = $9000
  2x = 3
  x = 1.5

Action: Answer("D")
Since the number of family members has to be a whole number, we can round up 1.5 to the nearest whole number, which is 2. Therefore, the total number of family members is 2x = 2 * 2 = 4.

  * If there are an even number of incomes, the median is the average of the two middle values.
  * If the median income is $3000, then there are at least three incomes, since the median is the second value when the incomes are listed in order.

  - Median is the middle value of a list of numbers.
  - If the median income is $3000, it means that half of the family members earn less than $3000 and half of the family members earn more than $3000.
  - We know the total income of the family is $9000.
  
Calculation:
  - If half the family earns less than $3000 and half the family earns more than $3000, then the total income earned by the half that earns less than $3000 is equal to the total income earned by the half that earns more than $3000.
  - Let's assume there are 'n' family members who earn less than $3000.
  - The total income earned by the half that earns less than $3000 is equal to n x 3000.
  - The total income earned by the half that earns more than $3000 is equal to (total number of family members - n) x 3000.
  - We know that the total income of the family is $9000, so we can set up an equation: n x 3000 + (total number of family members - n) x 3000 = 9000.
  - Solving for 'n', we get: 6000 = n x 3000, which means that n = 2.
  - If there are 2 family members who earn less than $3000, then there are 2 family members who earn more than $3000, so the total number of family members is 4.

Question: A starts a business with Rs.40,000. After 2 months, B joined him with Rs.60,000. C joined them after some more time with Rs.120,000. At the end of the year, out of a total profit of Rs.375,000, C gets Rs.150,000 as his share. How many months after B joined the business, did C join?
Choices:
  A: 2 months
  B: 4 months
  C: 23 months
  D: 24 months
  E: 84 months
Response 0:
Let's solve the problem using ratio and proportion:

The profit ratio of A, B, and C can be calculated based on their investment and time periods as follows:
Profit Ratio of A = (40000 x 12) months
Profit Ratio of B = (60000 x 10) months
Profit Ratio of C = (120000 x t) months, where t is the time period C invested.

We know that the total profit share of C is Rs. 150,000, which is equal to 150000/375000 = 2/5 of the total profit.

Therefore, the profit ratio of C is 2/5.
We can equate the profit ratios of A, B, and C and solve for t as follows:

Profit Ratio of A : Profit Ratio of B : Profit Ratio of C = 2 : 3 : 6t/100

2 : 3 : 6t/100 = 5 : 5 : 2  [Since C got 2/5 share of the total profit]

6t/100 = 4
t = 400/6
t = 66.67 months

C joined after B, who joined after 2 months. Therefore, C joined after 2 + 66.67 = 68.67 months, which is approximately equal to 69 months.

A:B:C = 8:10:2x

C's share = (375,000 * 2x) / (20x)
150,000 = (375,000 * 2x) / (20x)
x = 24

Therefore, C joined 24 months after B joined the business.

Question: The monthly salary S of a shop assistant is the sum of a fixed salary of $500 plus 5% of all monthly sales. What should the monthly sales be so that her monthly salary reaches $1500?
Choices:
  A: $50000
  B: $40000
  C: $30000
  D: $20000
  E: None of these
Response 0:

  The monthly salary S = 500 + 5% of monthly sales
  We want to find the monthly sale that will give S = $1500
  So, we need to solve the equation 1500 = 500 + 5% * monthly sales

Calculation: 
  1000 = 5% * monthly sales
  monthly sales = 1000 / 0.05 = $20000

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The monthly salary S of a shop assistant is the sum of a fixed salary of $500 plus 5% of all monthly sales. 
  We need to find the monthly sales that result in a monthly salary of $1500.
Calculation: 
  Let x be the monthly sales. 
  Then, the monthly salary will be S = 500 + 0.05x.
  We need to find the value of x that satisfies S = $1500.
  500 + 0.05x = 1500
  0.05x = 1000
  x = 1000/0.05 = $20000
Result:
  The monthly sales should be $20000.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 57 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The sum of k consecutive integers is 51. If the least integer is -50, then k =
Choices:
  A: 40
  B: 62
  C: 82
  D: 92
  E: 102
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If we have k consecutive integers, then their sum will be k times the average of those integers.
  If the least integer is -50, then the kth integer will be (-50 + (k-1)).
Action: 
  We can set up an equation using the above information: k * (-50 + (-50 + (k-1))) / 2 = 51.
  Simplifying, we get (k^2 - k - 102) = 0.
  Solving for k using the quadratic formula, we get k = (-(-1) +/- sqrt((-1)^2 - 4(1)(-102))) / 2(1).
  This simplifies to k = (1 +/- sqrt(409)) / 2.
  Since k must be a positive integer, we can see that k = (1 + sqrt(409)) / 2 ≈ 12.84.
  Therefore, the closest answer choice is C: 82. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  If we have k consecutive integers, starting from n, then their sum is k * n + (k * (k - 1)) / 2.
  We know that the least integer is -50, so the sum of k consecutive integers starting from -50 is:
  k * (-50) + (k * (k - 1)) / 2 = -50k + (k^2 - k) / 2 = (k^2 - 51k) / 2
  We also know that this sum is equal to 51.
  Therefore, we have the following equation:
  (k^2 - 51k) / 2 = 51
  Solving for k, we get:
  k^2 - 51k - 102 = 0
  Using the quadratic formula, we get:
  k = (51 ± sqrt(51^2 + 4 * 102)) / 2 = (51 ± 67) / 2
  Since we need a positive value of k, we choose k = (51 + 67) / 2 = 59.
Action: Answer("None of the Above") - The correct answer is not among the given choices. The correct answer is k = 59.
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  1. If n is an integer, then the sum of the first n positive integers is n*(n+1)/2.
  2. The sum of k consecutive integers is k times the average of the integers.
  3. If the least integer is -50, then the sum of k consecutive integers starting from -50 is (k*(-50 + (-50+k-1)))/2 = (k*(-100 + k - 1))/2 = (k*(k-101))/2.
  
Calculation:
  Using (2) and (3), we have (k*(k-101))/2 = 51 - (-50) = 101.
  Solving for k, we have k*(k-101) = 202.
  Factoring 202, we have 202 = 2*101.
  Since 101 is a prime number, the possible solutions for k are the divisors of 2*101, which are 1, 2, 101, and 202.
  However, k cannot be 1 or 2, because the sum of 1 or 2 consecutive integers cannot be 51.
  Therefore, the only possible solution for k is 101.
  
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  Let n be the first integer of the k consecutive integers. Then, the sum of the k consecutive integers is given by k * n + (k - 1) * k / 2.

  C: 5xy/(12w)

  E: 3y/(wx)

  - The rate of the liquid is w/25 gallons every x seconds
  - We need to find the time it takes for y gallons to pass through the drain
  - We can use the formula: Time = Amount / Rate
  
Calculations:
  - The rate of the liquid can be simplified to (w/x)/25 gallons per second
  - To convert the rate to gallons per minute, we multiply by 60: (w/x)/25 * 60 = 12w/5x gallons per minute
  - Using Time = Amount / Rate, we get Time = y / (12w/5x) = 5xy / (12w)

y gallons will take y*25/w*x seconds to pass through the drain, which is equal to y*5/(12w) minutes.

Question: A square piece of cloth is trimmed by 4 feet on one edge to form a rectangular piece, which is then cut diagonally in half to create two triangles. If the area of each of triangle is 70 square feet, what was the perimeter (in feet) of the original piece of square cloth?
Choices:
  A: 56
  B: 58
  C: 60
  D: 62
  E: 64
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The area of each triangle is 70 square feet, so their total area is 140 square feet.
  - Let x be the length of the original square piece of cloth. The area of the square is x^2. When 4 feet is trimmed off one edge, the rectangular piece has one side of length x-4 and the other of length x. The area of the rectangular piece is (x-4)x = x^2 - 4x.
  - Cutting the rectangular piece in half creates two congruent triangles. If we let h be the height of each triangle, then we have (x-4)h/2 = 70, so h = 140/(x-4).
  - Using the Pythagorean theorem, the length of the hypotenuse of each triangle is sqrt((x-4)^2 + h^2) = sqrt((x-4)^2 + 196/(x-4)^2).
Action: Answer("E")  
To solve for x, we can use the fact that the area of the square is equal to the sum of the areas of the triangles and the rectangular piece:
x^2 = 2(70) + x^2 - 4x
140 = x(2-4)
x = -70, which is clearly not a valid answer.
Thus, there is an error in the problem or the choices.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The area of a triangle can be calculated as A = (1/2) * b * h, where b and h are the base and height of the triangle, respectively.
  - The area of a square can be calculated as A = s^2, where s is the length of the side of the square.
  - The perimeter of a square can be calculated as P = 4s, where s is the length of the side of the square.
  - If a square piece of cloth is trimmed by 4 feet on one edge, the resulting rectangle will have one side that is 4 feet shorter than the other side.
  - If a rectangle is cut diagonally in half, the resulting triangles will be congruent.
  
Solution:
  Let s be the length of the side of the original square piece of cloth. After one edge of the square is trimmed by 4 feet, the resulting rectangle has dimensions s x (s-4). The area of the rectangle is A = s(s-4) = s^2 - 4s. Each of the resulting triangles has an area of 70 square feet, so the total area of the rectangle is 2 * 70 = 140 square feet. Therefore, we have the equation s^2 - 4s = 140. Rearranging, we get s^2 - 4s - 140 = 0. Factoring, we get (s-14)(s+10) = 0. Since s cannot be negative, the only valid solution is s = 14. Therefore, the original piece of cloth was a square with side length 14 feet, and its perimeter was P = 4s = 56 feet.

  - The diagonal of a rectangle divides it into two congruent right triangles.

Solution:
  - Let x be the length of one side of the original square.
  - After trimming 4 ft from one side, the dimensions of the rectangular piece become (x-4) ft x x ft.
  - The diagonal of the rectangular piece divides it into two congruent right triangles with legs x-4 and x.
  - The area of each triangle is 70 sq. ft, so using the area formula of a triangle, we get: 70 = 1/2 * (x-4) * x, which simplifies to x^2 - 4x - 140 = 0.
  - We can factor this equation as (x-14)(x+10) = 0, so x = 14 (since x cannot be negative).
  - Therefore, the original square piece of cloth had a side length of 14 ft, and its perimeter was 4 * 14 = 56 ft.

Action: Answer("A")

  - The area of a triangle = (1/2) * base * height.
  - The area of a square = side^2.
  - The perimeter of a square = 4 * side.
  
Let's assume that the side of the original square is "x". When we trim 4 feet of one edge, the new dimensions of the rectangular piece become (x-4) x x. When we cut this rectangle diagonally, we get two right triangles with base (x-4) and height x.

We know that the area of each of the two right triangles is 70 square feet. So we can write the following equation: 

(1/2) * base * height = 70
(1/2) * (x-4) * x = 70
x^2 - 4x - 140 = 0
(x-14)(x+10) = 0

Since x can't be negative, we know that x=14. Therefore, the side of the original square is 14 feet.

The perimeter of the original square is:
4 * side = 4 * 14 = 56 feet.

Response 9:
Let's assume the original side of the square piece of cloth is x feet. 

After trimming 4 feet, the rectangular piece will have a width of (x-4) feet and length of x feet. 

When this rectangular piece is cut diagonally in half, two triangles will be formed. We know that the area of each triangle is 70 square feet. Thus, 

(1/2) * base * height = 70 
=> base * height = 140 

Since the two triangles are identical, their bases and heights are the same. 

The base of each triangle is the length of the rectangular piece, which is x feet. 

The height of each triangle can be found using the Pythagorean theorem: 

height^2 = (x-4)^2 + x^2 
=> height^2 = 2x^2 - 8x + 16 

Since base * height = 140, we can substitute height in terms of x: 

x * sqrt(2x^2 - 8x + 16) = 140 

Squaring both sides: 

x^2 * (2x^2 - 8x + 16) = 19600 
=> 2x^4 - 8x^3 + 16x^2 - 19600 = 0 

Factoring out 2: 

2(x^4 - 4x^3 + 8x^2 - 9800) = 0 

Using the rational roots theorem, we can determine that x=10 is a root of the polynomial. 

Thus, the original square piece of cloth had a side length of 10 feet. 

Therefore, the perimeter of the original square piece of cloth = 4*10 = 40 feet. 

Action: Answer("40")

Response 2:
Knowledge:
  - The parking space is rectangular.
  - The length of the unpainted side is 9 feet.
  - The sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet.
  - We need to find the area of the rectangle.
  - We can use the formula for the area of a rectangle: area = length x width.

Solution:
  - Let's assume that the painted sides are x and y, and that the width of the rectangle is w.
  - We know that x + y + w = perimeter of the rectangle
  - If the unpainted side is 9 feet, then the painted sides have a combined length of 37 - 9 = 28 feet.
  - Therefore, x + y = 28.
  - We also know that the perimeter of a rectangle is 2 x length + 2 x width.
  - In this case, the length is (x + y), so 2(x + y) + 2w = x + y + w + 9.
  - Simplifying the equation, we get: x + y - w = 9.
  - Solving the system of equations {x + y = 28, x + y - w = 9} we find w = 19.
  - So the length of the rectangle is x + y = 28, and the width is w = 19.
  - The area of the rectangle is length x width = 28 x 19 = 532 square feet.

Choices:
  A: 30 feet
  B: 20 feet
  C: 10 feet
  D: 50 feet
  E: 60 feet
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's represent the length of the yard by 'x', because it is unknown. 
  The formula for the area of a rectangle is A = length x width.
  We know that one side of the yard is 100 feet wide, so the width is 100 feet.
  The total area of the yard is given as 3,000 square feet.
  We can use this information to set up an equation: 
  A = length x width
  3,000 = x(100)
  Divide both sides by 100: 3,000/100 = x
  Simplify: 30 = x
Action: Answer("A") 
Therefore, the other side of Julie's yard is 30 feet.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 63 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Hoses A and B spout water at different constant rates, and hose A can fill a certain pool in 8 hours. Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours and the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours. How many hours would it have taken hose B, working alone, to fill the entire pool?
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 15
  C: 12
  D: 6
  E: 3
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let's say hose A can fill the pool in x hours and hose B can fill the pool in y hours. 
  The formula to find how long it takes to fill the pool when both hoses are working together is: (1/x + 1/y) ^ (-1).
  If hose A fills the pool alone for t hours, that means that the fraction of the pool that hose A fills is t/x.
  The remaining fraction of the pool that hose B and A fill together is (1-t/x).
  We know that hose A fills the pool alone for 2 hours and both hoses working together fill the remaining fraction of the pool in 3 hours. 

Action: Answer("B") 

We can set up two equations with two unknowns based on the above knowledge:
  1. 2/x + 3(1/x + 1/y) = 1 (2 hours of hose A plus 3 hours of both hoses equals 1 pool)
  2. 1 - 2/x = 3(1/y) (the remaining fraction of the pool filled by hose B and A together is 1- 2/x)
  
Solving the first equation for y: 
  2/x + 3(1/x + 1/y) = 1
  2/x + 3/x + 3/y = 1
  3/y = 1 - 5/x
  y = 3x/(x-5)

Substituting y in the second equation:
  1 - 2/x = 3(1/y)
  1 - 2/x = 3((x-5)/(3x))
  1 - 2/x = (x-5)/x
  x = 10
  
Therefore, hose A can fill the entire pool in 8 hours, hose B can fill the entire pool in 15 hours. Hence the answer is "B".
Response 1:
Knowledge: This is a work problem. The formula used to solve work problems is W = R * T, where W represents the work done, R represents the rate of work, and T represents the time. We can also use the formula R = W / T to calculate the rate of work.
 
Let's assume that the entire pool requires P amount of work to fill.
If hose A can fill the pool alone in 8 hours, hose A's rate of work is P/8.
We can then set up the equation as follows:
(2/8)P + (3/8)PR = P
Simplifying this equation, we get:
5PR = 6P
Therefore, R, the rate of work for both hoses working together, is R = P/(5/6) = 6P/5

Now, we can use the formula R = W / T and the rate of hose A to find the rate of hose B.
P/8 + RB * 3 = P
RB = 5/24
Finally, we can use the rate of hose B to find the time it would take hose B to fill the pool alone. 
P/B = 1 / RB = Answer: 9.6 or approximately 10 hours. 

Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  Let's call the rate at which Hose A fills the pool "R_A", and the rate at which Hose B fills the pool "R_B". 
  We can use the formula: time = work/rate.
  In the first two hours, Hose A fills: 2 * R_A * 1 = 2R_A units of the pool.
  Therefore, the remaining work that the two hoses must do together is: 1 - 2R_A units of the pool.
  In the next three hours, the two hoses together can fill: 3 * (R_A + R_B) = 3R_A + 3R_B units of the pool.
  We can set up the following equation to solve for R_A: 
  2R_A + 3(R_A + R_B) = 1  (the total work is one full pool).
  Simplifying, we get: 5R_A + 3R_B = 1.
  We know that Hose A fills the pool in 8 hours, so R_A = 1/8.
Action: Answer("D")  
  Substituting R_A = 1/8 into the equation above, we can solve for R_B:
  5(1/8) + 3R_B = 1
  5/8 + 3R_B = 1
  3R_B = 3/8
  R_B = 1/8
  Therefore, Hose B fills the entire pool alone at a rate of 1/8, and it would take 8/1 = 8 hours for Hose B to fill the entire pool.
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  Let's suppose that hose A and hose B can fill the pool in "x" hours and "y" hours, respectively.
  The formula to calculate the amount of work done by a machine or a person is:
  Work = Rate × Time
  The formula to calculate the combined rate of two machines or persons working together is:
  Combined Rate = Rate of machine/person 1 + Rate of machine/person 2
  
Solution:
  Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours. Therefore, the amount of work done by hose A in 2 hours is:
  Work = Rate × Time
  Work = (1/8) × 2 = 1/4
  
  Let's denote the amount of work done by the two hoses working together to fill the pool in another 3 hours as "W". Then we can write:
  Combined Rate = Rate of hose A + Rate of hose B
  1/x + 1/y = W/5
  
  We can also write:
  W = Rate of hose A × Time + Rate of hose B × Time
  1 = (1/8) × 2 + (1/x + 1/y) × 3
  
  Substituting the value of W from the second equation into the first equation, we get:
  1/x + 1/y = (1 - 1/4) / 3 = 1/12
  
  We can solve this equation for y to get the rate of hose B, and then use the formula "Work = Rate × Time" to calculate the time it would take hose B to fill the pool alone.
  
  1/x + 1/y = 1/12
  1/y = 1/12 - 1/8 = 1/24
  y = 24
  
  Therefore, hose B can fill the entire pool alone in 24 hours.

  If hose A can fill a pool in 8 hours, its rate is 1/8 of the pool per hour.
  Let the rate of hose B be b.
  Together, the two hoses fill the pool at a rate of 1/8 + b.
  Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours, so it filled 2/8 of the pool.

  We can set up the equation (1/8 + b)t = 3/4, where t is the time it takes hose B to fill the pool alone.

  t = (3/4 - bt)/(1/8)

  1/8 + b = 1/4
  b = 1/4 - 1/8
  b = 1/8

  t = 6 - 8(1/8)
  t = 6 - 1
  t = 5

  Let's assume the pool can be filled with 1 unit of water.

  The first 2 hours, Hose A filled 2/8 = 1/4 of the pool. 
  The remaining 3/4 of the pool was filled in 3 hours by Hose A and Hose B working together. 
  Let x be the rate of Hose B, in unit of water per hour. Then the combined rate of Hose A and Hose B would be (1/8 + x) unit of water per hour. 
  We can set up the following equation to solve for x: 
  3/4 = (1/8 + x) * 3
Action: Answer("B") 

Calculations:
  3/4 = (1/8 + x) * 3
  3/4 = 3/8 + 3x
  3x = 3/4 - 3/8
  3x = 3/8
  x = 1/8
  Hose B's rate is 1/8 unit of water per hour. Therefore, it would take Hose B alone 8 hours to fill the entire pool. 

The correct answer is (A) 8.

  Let t be the number of hours it would take for hose B to fill the entire pool alone.
  Working alone, hose B can fill the remaining 3/4 units of the pool in t hours, so its fill rate is (3/4) / t units per hour.

  1/8 + x = 1/4
  Solving for x, we get x = 1/4 - 1/8 = 1/8
  Since the fill rate of hose B is 1/8 units per hour, we can write the following equation:
  (3/4) / (1/8) = 6
  Therefore, it would take hose B, working alone, 6 hours to fill the entire pool.

Choices:

  B: 33
  C: 35
  D: 42
  E: 58

  If a constant k is added or subtracted from each of the numbers, then the ratio of the numbers remains the same.
  
Let the two numbers be 3x and 5x, respectively.
After subtracting 9 from each, their new values are 3x - 9 and 5x - 9, respectively.
According to the problem, (3x-9)/(5x-9) = 12/23.

Solving the equation above, 
(3x-9)/(5x-9) = 12/23
69x - 207 = 60x - 108
9x = 99
x = 11

Therefore, the smaller number is 3x - 9 = 3(11) - 9 = 24.

  x = 99/3 = 33

Question: If one of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5, then what is the value of m?
Choices:
  A: -23.5
  B: -17.5
  C: -10.5
  D: -16.2
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Quadratic equation is of the form ax^2 + bx + c = 0.
  A quadratic equation has two roots.
  If one of the roots of the quadratic equation is given, then the other root can be determined.
  The sum of the roots of a quadratic equation is -b/a.
  The product of the roots of a quadratic equation is c/a.
  Here, a=1, c=22 and one of the roots is given as 1.5.
Action: 
  If one of the roots is 1.5, then the product of the roots is 22/1 = 22.
  Let the other root be r.
  Then, sum of the roots is 1.5 + r = -m/1 = -m.
  Therefore, 1.5 + r = -m.
  Also, 1.5*r = 22/1 = 22.
  Solving these equations, we get r= -29/3 and m= -10.5.
  Answer: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  A quadratic equation in the form of ax^2 + bx + c = 0 has two roots given by the formula (-b ± √(b^2 - 4ac)) / (2a).
  If (x - r) is a factor of a quadratic equation, where r is one of the roots of the equation, then the other root is given by the equation x = (c / r), where c is the constant term of the quadratic equation.
  
Using the given root, we can say that one of the factors of the quadratic equation is (x - 1.5). We can find the other factor by dividing the constant term 22 by the given root, which gives us the factor (x - 14.67). 

To find the value of m, we can either expand the product of the two factors or use the formula for sum and product of roots. 
The sum of the roots is -m/a, so -m = (1.5 + 14.67) = 16.17.
The product of the roots is c/a, so 22 = (1.5) * (14.67) - m, which gives m = -16.26.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 66 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In a large forest, 300 deer were caught, tagged, and returned during 2001. During 2002, 500 deer were caught at random, of which only 20 had tags from the previous year. If the percent of deer in the forest that had tags during the second year and were caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags, what is the total deer population in the forest (assuming no change in population between 2001 and 2002)?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 500
  C: 5000
  D: 6000
  E: 7500
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  There were 300 deer caught and tagged in year 1.
  During year 2, there were 500 deer caught randomly.
  Only 20 of the deer caught in year 2 had tags from year 1.
  We are assuming that the percent of deer in the forest with tags caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags.
  
Approach:
  We can use ratios to determine the total population.
  If 20 out of 500 deer caught in year 2 had tags, that means that the ratio of tagged deer to the total number of deer caught is 20/500 = 0.04.
  We can assume that this ratio is representative of the entire population.
  Therefore, if we let x be the total number of deer in the forest, then we know that 0.04x = 300 (the number of deer tagged in year 1).
  Solving for x, we get x = 7500.
  
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Let x be the total deer population in the forest. We know that 300 deer were caught, tagged, and returned during 2001, so the proportion of tagged deer at that time was 300/x. 

During 2002, 500 deer were caught at random, of which only 20 had tags from the previous year. We can set up the equation:

(300/x) = (20/500) 

This equation says that the proportion of tagged deer in the 2002 sample is equal to the proportion of tagged deer in the entire population. We can solve for x as follows:

300 * 500 = 20x
150000 = 20x
x = 7500

Therefore, the total deer population in the forest is 7500.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 69 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: By himself, Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours. On a particular day, he happens to finish two-thirds of the work. The remaining portion of the work is done by Jill, whose rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do. How long does it take Jill to finish the remaining work?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 8
  C: 22
  D: 50
  E: 20
Response 0:
Let's say the whole job is cleaning one yacht, and Jack can do this in 12 hours. Therefore, Jack's rate of work is 1/12 of the yacht per hour. 

On a particular day, Jack completes two-thirds of the job. Therefore, the remaining portion of the job that Jill does is one-third (1/3) of the whole job. 

Jill's rate of work is 5% of Jack's rate of work. Therefore, Jill's rate of work is: 5/100 x (1/12) = 1/240 of the yacht per hour. 

Let's say it takes Jill "t" hours to finish the remaining third of the job. 

We can write the equation below based on the work done by Jack and Jill: 

(2/3) = (1/12) x (total hours Jack worked) + (1/240) x t

Simplifying the equation above, we get: 

(2/3) = (t/2880) + (1/12)

Multiplying both sides by 2880, we get: 

(2/3) x 2880 = t + 240

Simplifying the equation above, we get: 

t = 1920/3 - 240 = 640 - 240 = 400

Therefore, it takes Jill 400 hours to finish the remaining third of the job. 

However, 400 hours seems like a very long time, so it's possible that there's an error in the calculation or the problem statement. 

Action: Answer("None of the Above")

  Jack's rate is 1/12 yacht per hour, so the amount of work he did is (2/3) * 1.
  Therefore, the amount of work left for Jill is x = (1/3) * 1 = 1/3 yacht.

  (1/3) = (1/240) * t
  t = (1/3) / (1/240) = 80

If Jack cleans the entire yacht in 12 hours, his rate of work is 1/12 of the yacht per hour.

Jill's rate of work is 5% of Jack's rate of work. So Jill's rate of work is (5/100) * (1/12) = 1/240 of the yacht per hour.

Let's use the formula "rate of work = amount of work ÷ time" to solve for "t". 
The amount of work is 1/3 of the yacht.
Jack finishes 2/3 of the yacht, which means he finishes (2/3) * (1/yacht per hour) * (12 hours) = 8 hours of work.
The remaining work that Jill has to do is (1/3) * (1/yacht per hour) * (12 hours) = 4 hours of work.
So we have:
  Jack's rate of work = 1/12 of the yacht per hour
  Jill's rate of work = 1/240 of the yacht per hour
  Jack's time = 8 hours
  Jill's time = t
  
 Jack's work + Jill's work = Total work
 (Jack's rate of work * Jack's time) + (Jill's rate of work * Jill's time) = (1/3) of the yacht
  
 ((1/12) * 8) + ((1/240) * t) = (1/3)
 (2/3) + ((1/240) * t) = (1/3)
 (1/240) * t = (1/3) - (2/3)
 (1/240) * t = (-1/3)
 t = (-1/3) ÷ (1/240) = (1/3) * (240/1) = 80

  On the particular day, Jack finishes two-thirds of the work, therefore the remaining one-third job will be completed by Jill.
  Jill's cleaning rate is just 5% of what Jack can do, therefore her per hour work rate is 5/100 * 1/J = 1/20J
  Jack's per hour work rate is 1/J
  Therefore, combined work rate of Jack and Jill is 1/J + 1/20J = 21/20J
  If Jack could finish the remaining one-third job in T hours, then we can conclude that
  two-thirds job can be done in 2/3 * J hours

Calculation:
  2/3 * J * 21/20J = 1
  14/20 = 1 - 21/20T
  21/20T = 6/20
  T = 6/20 * 20/21
  T = 6/21

Action: Answer("A") which is 4.

Choices:
  A: 22 hrs
  B: 18 hrs
  C: 16 hrs
  D: 20 hrs
  E: 13 hrs
Response 0:
Let's call the time it takes Mr. Sam to travel to the city by train "t" and the time it takes him to return by car "c". We know that t + c = 17 (total trip time is 17 hours) and (t-4) + (c-4) = 17 (he loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train).

Simplifying the second equation, we get t + c = 25. Solving the system of equations, we get c = 16 and t = 1. 

So, if Mr. Sam had traveled by car both ways, it would have taken him 16 hours.

Question: For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 3
  C: 2
  D: 1
  E: 0
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume that the coin diver brought 'c' copper coins and 'b' brass coins. 
  According to the problem statement, she gets 20 cents for each copper coin and 25 cents for each brass coin.
  So, her total earnings after one dive can be expressed as 20c + 25b.
  We are also given that the total earnings after one dive are $3.40.
  So we can write an equation: 20c + 25b = 340 cents.

Calculation:
  We need to find the minimum number of copper coins that she brought, which means we need to find the smallest possible value of 'c' that satisfies the above equation.
  Let's try to solve for 'c' in terms of 'b':
  20c + 25b = 340
  20c = 340 - 25b
  c = (340 - 25b)/20

  We know that the number of coins must be a whole number, so 'b' can only be 0, 1, 2, 3, or 4 (since if there were more brass coins, she would have earned more than $3.40).
  So we can try each value of 'b' and see which one gives a whole number for 'c':

  If b=0, then c = (340 - 25*0)/20 = 17
  If b=1, then c = (340 - 25*1)/20 = 16.75 (not a whole number)
  If b=2, then c = (340 - 25*2)/20 = 16.5 (not a whole number)
  If b=3, then c = (340 - 25*3)/20 = 16.25 (not a whole number)
  If b=4, then c = (340 - 25*4)/20 = 16

  So the minimum number of copper coins that she brought is 16.

- 20x + 25y = 340

Topic: Math
Question: The sum of the digits of a three digit number is 17, and the sum of the squares of its digits is 109. If we subtract 495 from the number, we shall get a number consisting of the same digits written in the reverse order. Find the number.

Topic: Math
Question: The ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is?
Choices:
  A: 2: π
  B: 7:2
  C: 8:2
  D: 6: π
  E: 8:3
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The volume of a cube is given by the formula V = s^3, where s is the length of a side of the cube.
  The volume of a sphere is given by the formula V = 4/3πr^3, where r is the radius of the sphere.
  The diameter of the sphere that fits inside the cube is equal to the length of a side of the cube.
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is given by V(cube)/V(sphere)

Action: 
  Let s be the side of the cube, then the diameter of the sphere would be s. 
  The radius of the sphere is r = s/2.
  V(cube) = s^3
  V(sphere) = 4/3π(s/2)^3 = 1/6πs^3
  V(cube)/V(sphere) = (s^3) / (1/6πs^3) = 6π
  Therefore, the ratio of the volumes of the cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is 6:π.
  Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The volume of a cube with side length "a" is given by a^3.
  - The volume of a sphere with radius "r" is given by (4/3)πr^3.
  - If a sphere fits perfectly inside a cube, then the diameter of the sphere is equal to the side length of the cube.
  - The diameter of the sphere is equal to twice the radius of the sphere.
  
Calculations:
  Let "a" be the side length of the cube.
  The diameter of the sphere which fits inside a cube is equal to "a".
  The radius of the sphere is equal to (1/2)a.
  The volume of the cube is a^3.
  The volume of the sphere is (4/3)π[(1/2)a]^3 = (1/6)πa^3.
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is (a^3)/[(1/6)πa^3] = (6/π).

Response 8:
Knowledge:
  The volume of a cube with side "a" is given by V_cube = a^3.
  The volume of a sphere with radius "r" is given by V_sphere = (4/3)πr^3.
  If a sphere is inscribed in a cube, the diameter of the sphere is equal to the edge of the cube.

To solve the question, we need to find the ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube.
Let "a" be the edge of the cube, and "r" be the radius of the inscribed sphere.
The diameter of the sphere is equal to the edge of the cube, so 2r = a.
We can substitute a = 2r in the equation for the volume of the cube: V_cube = a^3 = (2r)^3 = 8r^3.
We can substitute r = a/2 in the equation for the volume of the sphere: V_sphere = (4/3)πr^3 = (4/3)π(a/2)^3 = (1/6)πa^3.
The ratio of the volumes is V_cube : V_sphere = 8r^3 : (1/6)πa^3 = 48r^3 : πa^3.
We can substitute 2r for a to get the ratio in terms of "r": 48r^3 : πa^3 = 48r^3 : π(2r)^3 = 48r^3 : 8πr^3 = 6:π.

Response 9:

To solve this problem, we can find the ratio of the volume of the cube to the volume of the sphere that fits inside it.
Let s be the side length of the cube, and let r be the radius of the sphere.
Then, s = 2r, because the diameter of the sphere is equal to the side length of the cube.
The volume of the sphere is (4/3)πr^3, and the volume of the cube is s^3 = (2r)^3 = 8r^3.
So the ratio of the volumes is:
(8r^3) / ((4/3)πr^3) = 6π / 4 = 3π / 2.

Question: There are ten lime soda bottles on a table in a restaurant. They are to be served among two different groups of customers consisting of 5 members each. How many ways are there to create these 2 groups?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 105
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: 525
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  This question can be solved using combinations formula which is C(n,r) = n!/(r!*(n-r)!)
  In this case, we have 10 lime soda bottles to be divided into 2 groups of 5 members each.
  This is equivalent to selecting 5 bottles out of the total 10 bottles for the first group.
  The remaining 5 bottles will be for the second group.
  The formula to use is C(10,5) = 10!/(5!*5!) = 252
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  This is a combinatorics problem that can be solved using the formula for combinations.
  The formula for combinations is: C(n,r) = n!/r!(n - r)!

Action: 
The number of ways to choose 5 bottles out of 10 is given by 10! / (5! * 5!) = 252 / 120 = 21
After the first group is served, the remaining 5 bottles will go to the second group.
Therefore, the total number of ways to create these 2 groups is the number of ways to choose 5 bottles out of 10, which is 21.
Answer("D")
Response 9:
Knowledge: 
  This problem involves the concept of combinations, which represents the number of ways to choose k objects from a set of n distinct objects without regard to order. The formula for combinations is n choose k, which can be written as C(n,k) = n! / (k!*(n-k)!).
  
Action: 
  First, we need to determine the total number of ways to divide 10 lime soda bottles among two groups of 5 people each. This can be expressed as the number of ways to choose 5 bottles out of 10, which is C(10,5) = 10! / (5!*(10-5)!) = 252. However, since the two groups are indistinguishable (i.e., we don't care which group gets which set of bottles), we need to divide by 2 to avoid double-counting. Therefore, the answer is 252 / 2 = 126.
  
Therefore, the answer is (C) 126.

Topic: Math
Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  - The total number of files on Sam's hard drive is 250.
  - Let V be the number of files infected by a virus only, W be the number of files infected by a worm only, and B be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  - We know that W = 2.5B.
  - We also know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, which means that 50% were infected by a virus or both. This means that V + B = 0.5(250) = 125.
Action: 
  - We can use the fact that V + B = 125 to find B = 125 - V.
  - We can also use the fact that W = 2.5B.
  - The total number of files infected by a worm is W + B = 2.5B + B = 3.5B.
  - The total number of files infected by either a virus or a worm or both is V + W + B = V + 3.5B.
  - We know that V + 3.5B = 250 (since all files fall into these three categories).
  - Substituting B = 125 - V, we get V + 3.5(125 - V) = 250.
  - Solving for V, we get V = 25.
  - Therefore, B = 125 - V = 100.
  - The number of files NOT infected by a worm is 250 - (W + V + B) = 250 - (2.5B + V + B) = 250 - (2.5(100) + 25 + 100) = 75.
  - Answer: Answer("C") 75.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
- Let's call the number of files that are infected by only a virus "V", the number of files that are infected by only a worm "W", and the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm "VW".

- We know that V + W + VW = 250.
- We know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, so V + VW = (0.5)(250) = 125.

Action: 
- First, we can substitute VW = (2.5)W into the equation V + W + VW = 250 to get V + W + (2.5)W = 250, which simplifies to V + 3.5W = 250.
- Next, we can substitute V + VW = 125 into the equation V + 3.5W = 250 to get (125 - VW) + 3.5W = 250, which simplifies to W = 50.
- Finally, we know that the total number of files that were NOT infected by a worm is V + VW, which we already calculated to be 125. Therefore, the number of files that were NOT infected by a worm is 125.

  Selling Price = CP + 0.2CP = 1.2CP

2(4x) + 5(1x) = 210

Simplifying the equation:
8x + 5x = 210 / 2
13x = 105
x = 8.08 

The hotel orders 8 newspapers on each day of the week except Sunday, so it orders 2 * 8 = 16 newspapers on Sunday.

The hotel buys 15 newspapers on Monday since it buys 8 newspapers on Monday and it buys the same number of newspapers on each of the other days of the week.

  The cost per week is $210, so the cost of the Sunday papers is 4(2x) and the cost of the Monday to Friday papers is 1(x).
  The total cost is the sum of these, so we have the equation 4(2x) + 5(1x) = 210, which simplifies to 13x = 210.
  Solving for x, we get x = 16.15, which we round down to 16 since we cannot order a fraction of a newspaper.
Action: Answer("16")
Response 9:
Knowledge:
  The hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week.
  The hotel pays $4 for each Sunday paper and $1 for each paper on the rest of the days of the week.
  The hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers.
  
Let the number of papers on Sunday be s, and the number of papers on each of the other days of the week be d.
The total number of papers per week is s + 6d, since there are 7 days in a week and s is the number of papers on Sunday.
The total cost of the papers per week is 4s + 6d, since Sunday papers cost $4 and papers on the rest of the days cost $1.

Using the information above, we can set up two equations:
s + 6d = total number of papers per week
4s + 6d = $210, the total cost per week

We are asked to find the number of papers the hotel buys on Monday, which is the same as the number of papers the hotel buys on each of the other days of the week.

We can solve for d, the number of papers on each of the other days of the week, by first solving for s, the number of papers on Sunday:

4s + 6d = 210
s + 1.5d = 52.5
s = 52.5 - 1.5d

Substituting s = 2d into this equation, we get:

2d = 52.5 - 1.5d
3.5d = 52.5
d = 15

Therefore, the hotel buys 15 papers on each of the other days of the week, including Monday.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  * They meet for the second time when Allen has traveled twice the distance between X and Y and Bob has traveled thrice the distance between X and Y.
  * Let's assume the distance between X and Y is d.
  * If t is the time taken to travel from X to Y or from Y to X, then the total time taken for Allen to travel is (2t + (d/54)). Similarly, the total time taken for Bob is (2t + (d/78)).
  * We are given that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen while traveling the same distance between X and Y (i.e., d). This means that Bob travels (d + 48) km while Allen travels d km.

Let's try to form an equation by equating the total distances traveled by Allen and Bob.
Total distance traveled by Allen = distance traveled from X to Y + distance traveled from Y to X
= d + d = 2d

Total distance traveled by Bob = distance traveled from Y to X + distance traveled from X to Y + distance traveled from Y to X
= (d + 48) + d + (d + 48) = 3d + 96

We know that they meet for the second time when Allen has traveled twice the distance between X and Y and Bob has traveled thrice the distance between X and Y.
So, the time taken by Allen to travel twice the distance between X and Y is equal to the time taken by Bob to travel thrice the distance between X and Y.

Equating the time taken by Allen and Bob, we get:
(2t + (d/54)) = (3t + ((d + 48)/78))

Simplifying the above equation, we get:
t = (22/37) hours

We can now use the value of t to calculate the distance between X and Y.
d = speed x time
   = 54 x (22/37)
  = 32 km

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  When two objects move towards each other, the distance relative to one another decreases at the sum of their speeds.
  When two objects move away from each other, the distance relative to one another increases at the difference of their speeds.

Let's say the distance between X and Y is d km.
Let's say they meet for the second time after t hours since they started.
When they meet for the first time, they would have together covered a distance of d km since they started.
When they meet for the second time, the distance covered by Allen is d km, and the distance covered by Bob is 2d + 48 km.
Let's say Allen started at time t=0 from X. When he covers the distance d km to reach Y, the time taken is d/54 hours.
At this point, Bob has covered (d + 48) km. Since he is traveling at 78 kmph, the time taken to cover this distance is (d + 48)/78 hours.
Since they both started at the same time, they meet at time t = d/54 = (d+48)/78.
Solving for d, we get d = 126 km.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Let the distance between X and Y be d. 
Let the time taken by both Allen and Bob to meet for the second time be t. 

When they meet for the first time, let's suppose Allen has traveled x km and Bob has traveled (d-x) km. 
Time taken by Allen to cover x km = x/54 
Time taken by Bob to cover (d-x) km = (d-x)/78 

Since they start at the same time and meet at the same point, 
x/54 = (d-x)/78 
Solving this equation, we get: x = 18d/65 

When they meet for the second time, let's suppose Allen has traveled y km from Y towards X. 
Then Bob has traveled (d-(y+48)) km from X towards Y. 
Time taken by Allen to cover y km = y/54 
Time taken by Bob to cover (d-(y+48)) km = (d-(y+48))/78 

Since they meet for the second time, they have covered the same distance: 
y + (d-(y+48)) = d + x 
Solving this equation, we get: y = (79d-2304)/325 

Now, we can substitute the value of x and y to find the distance d: 
(d-x) + 48 = (y+48) 
Substituting x and y, we get: 
d - 18d/65 + 48 = (79d-2256)/325 + 48 
Simplifying this equation, we get: 
d = 126 km 

Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 126 km.

t2 = (d + 48)/78

distance = speed * time
X to meeting point distance = d
Meeting point to X distance = d

t3 = t4

2d/54 = (2d + 48)/78
d = 72

  During the forward journey: d = s x 6
  During the return journey: d = (s + 12) x 4
  
Solution:
  We can use the above equations to solve for "d". 
  From the first equation, we can get: s = d/6
  Substituting s in the second equation, we get: d = (d/6 + 12) x 4
  Solving for d, we get: d = 144 km.

Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The number of water lilies doubles every two days.
  - It takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies if there is one water lily initially.
  - We want to find how many days the lake will be fully covered with lilies if initially there were 64 water lilies on it.

Solution:
  If there is one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days to be fully covered. This means that after 58 days, there will be half of the lake covered, or 2^(58-1) = 2^57 water lilies on the lake.
  
  If initially there were 64 water lilies, then after 58 days there will be:
  2^57 - 64 water lilies left to double until the lake is fully covered. We can solve for this using the equation:
  2^(t/2) = 2^57 - 64, where t is the number of days left until the lake is fully covered.

  Solving for t, we get:
  t/2 = log2(2^57 - 64)
  t = 2*log2(2^57 - 64)

Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Train M travels from City A to City B and takes 4 hours to complete the journey.
  Train N travels from City B to City A and takes 3.5 hours to complete the journey.
  The two trains are moving towards each other and will meet at some point in between the two cities.
  We can use the formula distance = speed x time to solve this problem.
  
Action: Answer("B") 
  The time difference between the departure of train M and train N is 2 hours (7am - 5am).
  In this time, train M travels a distance of 2 x speed of M (since it covers the distance it would have covered in 2 hours), and
  Train N travels a distance of 2 x speed of N.
  The total distance both trains cover is the distance between City A and City B.
  Let's say the distance between City A and City B is D.
  Therefore, the distance covered by M = 2 x speed of M = (D/4) x 2 = D/2
  The distance covered by N = 2 x speed of N = (D/3.5) x 2 = 4D/7
  The total distance covered by both trains = D/2 + 4D/7 = 15D/14
  The time taken for both trains to meet = distance / combined speed of the trains
  The combined speed = speed of train M + speed of train N
  The speed of train M = distance / time taken = D/4
  The speed of train N = distance / time taken = D/7.5
  The combined speed = (D/4) + (D/7.5) = 23D/60
  Time taken = (15D/14) / (23D/60) = 30/23 hours
  This can be converted to 1 hour 18.26 minutes, which is approximately equal to 1 hour 15 minutes.
  Therefore, the answer is B.

  Distance traveled by Train N = Speed of Train M * Time taken by Train N

  Distance traveled by Train M = Speed of Train M * Time taken by Train M
  Distance traveled by Train N = Speed of Train N * Time taken by Train N

  Distance traveled by Train N = (d / 8) + (t - 7) * d / 3.5

  (d / 8) + (4 - t) * d / 4 = (d / 8) + (t - 7) * d / 3.5

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 84 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Average (arithmetic mean) is the sum of all the numbers divided by the total count of numbers.
  The new average weight is 2.6 tons more than the old average weight.
  We are given the count of vehicles that is 10 and the old average weight, which is 12.2 tons.
Calculation:
  The sum of the original 10 vehicles is 10 * 12.2 = 122 tons.
  Let x be the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck.
  The new total weight is (122 + x) tons.
  The new average weight is (122 + x) / 11.
  The new average weight is 12.2 + 2.6 = 14.8 tons.
  (122 + x) / 11 = 14.8
  122 + x = 11 * 14.8
  122 + x = 162.8
  x = 40.8
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The formula for the arithmetic mean is:
  mean = (sum of observations) / (number of observations)
  We can use this formula to solve the problem.
  Let x be the weight of the new heavy duty truck in tons.
  We have the following equation (from the problem statement):
  12.2 = (sum of weights of the 10 vehicles) / 10
  After the new truck is added, the new average is:
  12.2 + 2.6 = (sum of weights of the 10 vehicles + x) / 11
  We can use these two equations to solve for x.

Calculation:
  Multiply both sides of the first equation by 10 to get:
  sum of weights of the 10 vehicles = 122
  Multiply both sides of the second equation by 11 to get:
  11 * 14.8 = sum of weights of the 10 vehicles + x
  162.8 = 122 + x
  x = 40.8

  - The weight of the heavy duty truck is 162.8 - 122 = 40.8 tons.

Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Knowledge:
- The amount of sand in the initial mixture is 30% of 10kg, which is 0.3*10 = 3kg.
- The amount of clay in the initial mixture is 70% of 10kg, which is 0.7*10 = 7kg.
- To make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand, we need to add 3kg of sand and remove 3kg of clay.
- Let x be the amount of mixture to be removed and replaced with pure sand.
- The amount of sand in the new mixture will be (3+x)kg, which will be 50% of the new mixture.
- The amount of clay in the new mixture will be (7-x)kg, which will also be 50% of the new mixture.

Action:
- In the initial mixture, the amount of sand is 3kg, which is 30% of 10kg. This means that the amount of clay is 7kg, which is 70% of 10kg.
- To make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand, we need to remove and replace (7-3)kg = 4kg of the mixture with pure sand.
- Let x be the amount of mixture to be removed and replaced with pure sand. In the new mixture, the amount of sand will be (3+x)kg and the amount of clay will be (7-x)kg.
- Since we are removing 4kg of the initial mixture, the amount of the new mixture will be 10kg - 4kg = 6kg.
- The amount of sand in the new mixture will be 50% of 6kg, which is 3kg. This means that we need to add 3-3 = 0kg of sand.
- The amount of mixture to be removed and replaced with pure sand is x = 4kg.
- Therefore, the answer is 4/7, which is choice A. Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
Let's assume that the total quantity of mixture is 'M' kilograms. 
The mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay, hence the amount of sand in the mixture is 0.3M and the amount of clay in the mixture is 0.7M.
In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand, the sand content has to be increased by 20% (i.e. 50% - 30%). 
On the other hand, the clay content has to be decreased by 20% (i.e. 70% - 50%).

Calculation:
If 'x' kilograms of the mixture is removed and replaced with pure sand, then the new quantity of sand in the mixture is (0.3M - 0.2x + x) and the new quantity of clay in the mixture is (0.7M - 0.5x).
Since the new mixture contains equal quantities of sand and clay, we have:
0.3M - 0.2x + x = 0.7M - 0.5x
Simplifying this equation, we get:
0.3M + 0.3x = 0.7M
0.4M = 0.3x
x = 4M/3

Therefore, we need to remove and replace 4M/3 kilograms of the mixture with pure sand.

Approximately, 4M/3 = 4*(10/3) = 40/3 which is closest to option D.

Question: Find the total no. of distinct bike no.'s that can beformed using 2 letters followed by 2 no.'s. How many letters need to be distinct?
Choices:
  A: 74453
  B: 64543
  C: 74325
  D: 65000
  E: 97656
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  To form a bike number, we need to use 2 letters followed by 2 digits.
  We have 26 letters from A to Z.
  We have 10 digits from 0 to 9.
  We can use the permutation formula to calculate the total number of distinct bike numbers possible.
  The formula is P(n,r) = n! / (n-r)!
  Here, n=36 (26 letters and 10 digits) and r=4 (2 letters and 2 digits).
  Total no. of distinct bike numbers possible = P(36,4) = 36 x 35 x 34 x 33 = 45,697,080
  
  For the second part of the question, we need to find out how many letters need to be distinct.
  To calculate this, we can use the permutation formula again.
  We need to select 2 letters out of 26 and arrange them in 2 positions. The digits can be repeated.
  So, n=26 and r=2.
  Number of ways to select and arrange 2 distinct letters = P(26,2) = 26 x 25 = 650

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 88 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of all sides of the rectangle.
  In this case, we are given that the perimeter is 340 meters.
  We can use the perimeter to find the dimensions of the rectangle.
  Then, we can use the dimensions to find the area of the rectangle.
  The area of the rectangular plot, along with the 1-meter broad boundary around it, will give us the area that needs to be gardened.
  The cost of gardening per square meter is given as 10.
  
Calculation:
  Let's first find the dimensions of the rectangle.
  Perimeter = 2*(Length + Breadth)
  340 = 2*(L+B)  => L+B = 170
  Let's assume the length of the rectangle is x meters.
  So, the breadth will be (170 - x).
  Now, we can find the area of the rectangle as: A = L*B
  A = x(170 - x)
  A = 170x - x^2
  We need to add the area of the 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot.
  The length of the rectangle with the boundary will be (x+2) meters.
  The breadth of the rectangle with the boundary will be [170 - (x+2)] = (168 - x) meters.
  So, the area of the rectangle with the boundary will be:
  (x+2)(168 - x)
  A = (168x - x^2 + 336 - 2x)
  A = -x^2 + 166x + 336

  The cost of gardening per square meter is given as 10.
  So, the total cost will be the area multiplied by the cost per square meter.
  Total Cost = A * 10
  Total Cost = (-x^2 + 166x + 336) * 10
  Total Cost = -10x^2 +1660x + 3360

  2 x (length + breadth) = 340
  length + breadth = 170
  Let the length be x and the breadth be y.
  x + y = 170 - Equation 1
  Length of 1-meter boundary = x + 2 + y + 2 = x + y + 4
  Breadth of 1-meter boundary = x + 2 + y + 2 = x + y + 4
  Area of 1-meter boundary = (x + y + 4) x (x + y + 4)
  Area of 1-meter boundary = (x + y)² + 8(x + y) + 16
  Area of 1-meter boundary = (170 - 4)² + 8(170 - 4) + 16
  Area of 1-meter boundary = 168² + 8*166 + 16
  Area of 1-meter boundary = 28224
  Cost of gardening around the rectangular plot = 28224 x 10
  Cost of gardening around the rectangular plot = 282240

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Let's first represent the ages of Joe, his sister, and his father with variables. Let's use "J" for Joe's age, "S" for his sister's age, and "F" for his father's age. 

From the first sentence of the problem, we know that:

J + S + F = 100 

From the second sentence of the problem, we know that when Joe is as old as his father:

J + F = 2(S)

We can simplify this equation to:
J = 2S - F 

From the third sentence of the problem, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. We can represent this with the following equation:

F = 2(S - F)

Simplifying and solving for S, we get:

S = 2F/3

Now we can substitute this expression for S into our first equation:

J + S + F = 100 

J + 2F/3 + F = 100 

Multiplying both sides of the equation by 3 to eliminate the fraction:

3J + 2F + 3F = 300 

3J + 5F = 300 

Substituting J = 2S - F, we get:

3(2S - F) + 5F = 300 

6S - 3F + 5F = 300 

6S + 2F = 300 

Substituting S = 2F/3, we get:

6(2F/3) + 2F = 300 

4F = 225 

F = 56.25 

Therefore, Joe's father is 56.25 years old.

Answer: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Let's assume that Joe's age is J, his sister's age is S, and his father's age is F. 

From the first statement, we know that J + S + F = 100. 

From the second statement, we know that when J = F, S + (J - F) = 2S, which simplifies to J = S. So, we can replace S with J in the first two equations. 

From the third statement, we know that when J = F, F = 2(S - (F - S)), which simplifies to F = 3S/2. 

Now we have two equations with two variables: 
J + J + 3S/2 = 100  (using F = 3S/2 and replacing S with J)
S = J 

Solving these equations, we get:
J = 25 
S = 25 
F = 50 

So the age of Joe's father is 50. 

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume Joe's age as J, Joe's sister's age as S and Joe's father's age as F.
  We have two equations:
  J + S + F = 100  ---(1)
  J + F = 2 * (S)  ---(2)
  When Joe is as old as his father, we can write the following equations:
  J + F = 2 * (S + F - J)  ---(3)
  Solving the equations (1), (2) and (3), we can find the age of Joe's father.

Solution:
  From equation (2), we can write S = (J + F)/2
  Substituting S in equation (1),
  J + (J + F)/2 + F = 100
  2 * J + F = 100 - F
  3 * J + 2 * F = 100  ---(4)
  Substituting S in equation (3),
  J + F = 2 * ((J + F)/2 + F - J)
  J + F = 2 * F
  J = F  ---(5)
  Substituting (5) in equation (4),
  3 * J + 2 * J = 100
  5 * J = 100
  J = 20
  Substituting J in equation (5),
  F = J
  F = 20

x + y + z = 100  (Equation 1)

From the second sentence, we know that:
When x = z, y + (z - x) = 2y
Simplifying this, we get:
z - x = y  (Equation 2)

From the third sentence, we know that:
When x = z, z = 2(y - (z - y))
Simplifying this, we get:
3z - 4y = 0  (Equation 3)

Now we have three equations and three variables, which we can solve simultaneously to find z (the age of Joe's father).

First, we can substitute Equation 2 into Equation 1 to eliminate y:
x + (z - x) + z = 100
2z = 100
z = 50

Then, we can substitute z = 50 into Equation 3 to solve for y:
3(50) - 4y = 0
150 - 4y = 0
4y = 150
y = 37.5

Finally, we can use Equation 2 to solve for x:
50 - x = 37.5
x = 12.5

So Joe's father is currently 50 years old.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge: When the coin is flipped:
  - If it lands on Heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan.
  - If it lands on Tails, Jonathan will give $3 to Christopher.
  After 20 coin flips:
  - If neither won or lost any amount, Christopher's gains must be equal to Jonathan's losses.
  - The difference between the amount of Heads and Tails determines the net gain or loss.
    - If the amount of Heads and Tails is equal, the net gain or loss is zero.
    - If the amount of Heads is greater than Tails, the net gain is positive.
    - If the amount of Tails is greater than Heads, the net gain is negative.
    
Action: Answer("E")  
Explanation: 
- Let H be the number of times the coin landed on Heads.
- Then the number of times the coin landed on Tails is 20 - H.
- Christopher will gain 2 dollars H times, so his total gain is $2H.
- Jonathan will lose 3 dollars (20 - H) times, so his total loss is $3(20 - H) = $60 - $3H.
- Since neither won or lost any amount, we have:
  - Christopher's gains = Jonathan's losses
  - $2H = $60 - $3H
  - 5H = 60
  - H = 12.
- Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times. Answer("E").
Response 1:
Knowledge:
- If the coin landed heads $x$ times in 20 flips, then Christopher would give Jonathan $2x.
- If the coin landed tails $y$ times in 20 flips, then Jonathan would give Christopher $3y.
- Christopher and Jonathan did not win or lose any amount, so the total amount given by Christopher was equal to the total amount given by Jonathan.

Let's solve the problem:
- Let's assume that the coin landed heads $x$ times and tails $y$ times.
- Christopher gave Jonathan $2x$ dollars, and Jonathan gave Christopher $3y$ dollars.
- According to the problem, $2x = 3y$.
- Since 20 coin flips were made, we have $x + y = 20$.
- We can simplify the first equation to $y = \frac{2}{3}x$.
- Substituting this equation into $x + y = 20$ gives $x + \frac{2}{3}x = 20$.
- Solving for $x$, we get $x = 12$.

Action: Answer("E")

Action: Answer("10")  
If the coin landed on Heads x times, then it landed on Tails (20-x) times.
Christopher will give $2 for every Head, so the total amount of money he will give to Jonathan is 2x.
Jonathan will give $3 for every Tails, so the total amount of money he will give to Christopher is 3(20-x).
Since neither of them won any money, then: 
2x=3(20-x) 
2x= 60-3x
5x=60
x=12
So, the coin landed on Heads 12 times, and since the total number of coin flips is 20, it landed on Tails (20-12=8) times. 
Therefore, Answer("A") is correct.

Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The formula to calculate distance is distance = speed * time
  - Let's call the distance from A to B "x"
  - Let's call the time it takes Kevin to travel from A to B "t1"
  - Let's call the time it takes Kevin to return from B to A "t2"
  - We know that Kevin traveled at 70 mph from A to B and 90 mph from B to A
  
From the problem:
  - During the last 3 hours of the trip Kevin was still approaching B, 70 miles away from it
  - Therefore, it took Kevin (x - 70) miles to travel from B to A during the last 3 hours of the trip
  - We can use this information to create an equation that relates the distance from A to B with the travel times:
  
    x = 70 * t1  (distance from A to B)
    x = 90 * t2 + 70  (distance from B to A, plus the 70 miles Kevin traveled during the last 3 hours of the trip)
    
  - We can solve for t1 and t2 by setting the two equations equal to each other:
  
    70 * t1 = 90 * t2 + 70
    7 * t1 = 9 * t2 + 7
    
  - We know that Kevin's total travel time was t1 + t2, and we also know that he was traveling for 3 hours less than the total travel time when he was 70 miles away from B:
  
    t1 + t2 - 3 = (x - 70) / 90
    
  - We can now solve for x by substituting t1 and t2 in the last equation and solving for x:
  
    t1 = (9/16) * (x/70 - 1/9)
    t2 = (7/16) * (x/90 - 7/9)
    
    x = 900
    
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  In the first part of the trip, Kevin travels from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph.
  In the second part of the trip, Kevin travels from B to A at a constant speed of 90 mph.
  Exactly 3 hours before the end of the trip, Kevin was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. 

Let's use d to denote the distance between A and B. 

In the first part of the trip, Kevin's travel time is t1 = d/70. 

In the second part of the trip, Kevin's travel time is t2 = d/90. 

So his total travel time is: 
t1 + t2 = d/70 + d/90 = 9d/630 + 7d/630 = 16d/630 

The remaining three hours of travel time is spent in the second part of the trip, so his travel time in the second part of the trip is t2 - 3 = (d/90) - 3. 

We know that, at that time, he was 70 miles away from B, so the remaining distance between B and A is d - 70. 

So we can use the formula: 
rate = distance / time 

to write: 

70 = (d-70)/(d/90 - 3)

Solving this equation gives d = 270.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Distance = Speed x Time
  Kevin drove at 70 mph from A to B and at 90 mph from B to A.
  Since the distance from A to B is the same as the distance from B to A, we'll denote the distance between A and B as "d".
  We know that he was 70 miles away from B, 3 hours before the end of his trip.

Action:
  Let's start by calculating the time it took for Kevin to reach 70 miles away from B.
  Let's denote the time it took Kevin to reach 70 miles away from B as "t".
  We know that Distance = Speed x Time
  So, t = Distance / Speed
  t = 70 / 70
  t = 1
  
  This means that it took Kevin 1 hour to reach 70 miles away from B. 
  Since he was 3 hours away from the end of his trip at this point, he had 3 more hours of driving time. 

  Let's calculate how far he drove from that point to A.
  We know that his speed at that point was 90 mph, and he had 3 more hours of driving time.
  So, Distance = Speed x Time
  Distance = 90 x 3
  Distance = 270
  
  This means that he drove 270 miles from 70 miles away from B to A.
  Therefore, the total distance between A and B is:
  Distance = The distance he drove from A to B + The distance he drove from B to A
  Distance = d + d
  Distance = 2d
  
  We know that the distance he drove from 70 miles away from B to A is 270 miles.
  So: 
  2d - 270 = d
  d = 270
  
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 270 miles.

  - Let t2 be the time it takes Kevin to travel from B to A at 90 mph.

    - (70 mph + 90 mph) / 2 = 80 mph
  - We know that exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  - Therefore, 3 hours before the end of the trip, Kevin had traveled for (T - 3) hours, where T is the total duration of the trip.
  - We can set up the equation:
    - 70 mph * (T - 3) = d - 70

Action: Answer("D")  
Solution:

  - We also know that the average speed for the entire trip is 80 mph, and the distance is d.
  - Therefore, we can use the formula d = r * t to get another equation:
    - d = 80 mph * T
  - We can substitute this expression for d in the first equation, and solve for T:
    - 70 mph * (T - 3) = 80 mph * T - 70
    - 70 mph * T - 210 = 80 mph * T - 70
    - 10 mph * T = 140
    - T = 14 hours
  - Now that we know the total duration of the trip is 14 hours, we can use the formula d = r * t with either of the speeds to find the distance:
    - d = 70 mph * (14 hours / 2) = 490 miles
  - Therefore, the distance between A and B is 490 miles, which corresponds to choice D.

  - Solving for x, we get: x = 180 miles.

Topic: Math
Question: I know a 5 digit number having a property that with a 1 after it, it is three times as large as it would be with a 1 before it.
What is that number?
Choices:
  A: 42857
  B: 32456
  C: 76523
  D: 24567
  E: 43566
Response 0:
Let the 5 digit number be represented by abcde, where a, b, c, d, and e are digits.
According to the problem statement, with a 1 after it, the number becomes 10 times larger than the original number plus 1. This can be represented as 100000a + 10000b + 1000c + 100d + 10e + 1 = 3(10000a + 1000b + 100c + 10d + e + 1).
Simplifying this equation, we get 29999a = 2997e + 299b + 30c + 2d.
Since 29999 is not divisible by 2, 3, 5, or 10, e must be an odd digit. Also, the left side of the equation is divisible by 7, so the right side must also be divisible by 7. This means that 2d + 3c - b must be divisible by 7. Checking the odd digits for e, we find that e = 3 gives a solution with d = 6, c = 5, b = 2, and a = 1.
Therefore, the 5-digit number is 12363.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

Action:

- Multiplying 1abcde by 3 gives us 3abcde.
- We know that a1bcde is also three times as large as abcde, so a1bcde = 3*abcde.
- Substituting a1bcde by 3*abcde in the equation 1abcde * 3 = a1bcde, we get: 1abcde * 3 = 3*abcde.
- Simplifying the equation, we have abcde = 2*edcba.
- Since the number has 5 digits, we know that a and e must be odd numbers (otherwise 2*edcba would not be a 5-digit number).
- We also know that a < 2, because otherwise 2*edcba would have 6 digits.
- Trying out odd numbers for a and e, we find that a=1 and e=3 satisfy the conditions.
- Therefore, the number is 12345*2 = 24690.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Let's assume that there are "n" employees in the organization.
From the given information, we can set up the following two equations:
1. n*x = 600000   .....(1)   (where x represents the amount each employee would contribute)
2. n*(x+60) = 624000 .....(2) 

Now, we can solve for "n", by solving the above two equations simultaneously.
Multiplying equation (1) by (x+60) on both sides, we get:
nx + 60n = 624000

Substituting the value of nx from equation (1) into the above equation, we get:
600000 + 60n = 624000
60n = 24000
n = 400

Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Let's assume there are 'n' employees in the organization.
Total amount collected by equal contribution = Rs. 6,00,000
Contribution by each employee = Total amount / Number of employees
Contribution by each employee = 600000/n

Total amount collected by contribution of Rs.60 extra by each employee = Rs. 6,24,000
Contribution by each employee including Rs.60 extra = (600000/n) + 60

Now, as per question stated - 
(600000/n) + 60 = 624000/n

On solving above equation, we get:
n = 400

Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.

  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800

Therefore, each daughter will receive 4x and each son will receive 5x.

Simplifying the equation, we get:
8x + 25x + 4x = 8600

So, each daughter will receive 4x = Rs. 928

Therefore, the answer is: Answer("D") Rs. 700.
